## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship for a material. Temperature typically modifies the elastic modulus or introduces thermal softening, while strain may enter linearly (elastic) or as a power-law (plastic hardening).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (isothermal): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at constant T)
- Thermoelastic Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (linear elasticity with thermal stress)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T) (stress from total strain minus thermal strain)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies linearly with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (modulus with higher-order T dependence)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law softening with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined)
- Nonlinear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (polynomial with cross-coupling)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or (1 - c1*T**c2) multiplying the strain-dependent term
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermal softening at high T → homologous temperature terms like (1 - (c0*T)**c1) or exponential decay exp(-c*T)
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → sum of linear term c0*epsilon and nonlinear term c1*epsilon**c2 capturing both regimes
- Strain-temperature cross-coupling → product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 reflecting thermomechanical interaction
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius form exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0*T) for diffusion-controlled deformation
- Modulus degradation → ratio or polynomial in T multiplying the entire stress expression as a prefactor
- Compressive vs tensile asymmetry → odd powers of epsilon or terms involving epsilon*Abs(epsilon)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)
Candidate formulas: 58

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT: 90.776·ε² + 2.482·(T - 337.769)·log(ε + 1)**

Expanding: **90.776·ε² + 2.482·T·log(ε+1) - 839.029·log(ε+1)**

So the GT has three functional components:
1. ε² term
2. T·log(ε+1) term
3. log(ε+1) term

Let me check candidates systematically for those that can produce these three terms.

**Candidate 1:** T·c0·ε + c1·ε² + c2·ε + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·ε + c6·ε·log(c4·ε+1)
Has T·ε (linear in T and ε), but GT needs T·log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 10:** T·c0·ε + c1·ε·exp(T·c2) + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·ε^c6
Setting c0=0, c2=0: c1·ε + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·ε^c6. No T·log term. No match.

**Candidate 16:** T·c0·ε + T·c1 + c2·ε + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·log(c6·ε+1)
Has T·c0·ε and T·c1 but no T·log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 41:** T·c0·ε² + c1·ε^c2 + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·ε + c6·ε²
Has T·ε² but needs T·log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 55:** T·c0 + T·c1·(c2+ε)^(1/3) + c3·log(c4·ε+1) + c5·ε + c6·ε²
Needs T·(c2+ε)^(1/3) to become T·log(ε+1). Can't match - different functional forms.

**Candidate 49:** T·c0·(c1+ε)^(1/3) + c2·log(c3·ε+1) + c4·log(c5·ε+1) + c6·ε + c7·ε²
Same issue with cube root vs log.

**Candidate 50:** T²·c0·ε/(T·c1+c2) + T·c3·ε/(T·c1+c2) + T·c4·ε/(T·c1+c2) + T·c5·log(c6·ε+1)/(T·c1+c2) + c7·ε/(T·c1+c2) + c8·log(c6·ε+1)/(T·c1+c2) + c9·ε/(T·c1+c2)

If c1=0, c2=1: T²·c0·ε + T·c3·ε + T·c4·ε + T·c5·log(c6·ε+1) + c7·ε + c8·log(c6·ε+1) + c9·ε

Setting c0=0, c3=0, c4=0: T·c5·log(c6·ε+1) + c8·log(c6·ε+1) + (c7+c9)·ε

This gives T·log and log terms but no ε². No match.

**Candidate 54:** T·c0·ε^c1 + c2·ε^c3 + c4·log(c5·ε+1) + c6·ε^c1

Setting c1=0: T·c0 + c2·ε^c3 + c4·log(c5·ε+1) + c6. No T·log term. 

But wait - what if c1 is chosen differently? We need T·log(ε+1) which can't come from T·ε^c1.
